What happens if ITS Facilities Services determines that a vehicle will be suplused? All decals, etc., except for inspection and registration stickers, must be removed and the vehicle cleaned inside and out. None When ITS Facilities Services decides to surplus a vehicle, they follow specific procedures to ensure a smooth transition. The vehicle is first removed from service, and all related items such as gas cards, Fleet Service cards/manuals, E-ZPass tags, and completed/signed mileage reports are also turned in. The vehicle is then transported to the Swan Street location if it wasn't originally assigned parking in Albany/Capital District. Once turned in to ITS Facilities Services, all related items are processed for auction, transfer, or disposal by filling out a Report of Surplus Motor Vehicles and Motorized Equipment, CS-201.1 Form. ITS Facilities Services will then notify all concerned parties that the vehicle is no longer in service. 4 The reference answer outlines several key steps when a vehicle is to be surplused: 1) All decals, except for inspection and registration stickers, must be removed, and the vehicle must be cleaned inside and out. 2) The vehicle is transported to the Swan Street location if it is not normally parked in Albany/Capital District. 3) When the vehicle is turned in, all related items such as gas cards, Fleet Service cards/manuals, E-ZPass tags, and completed/signed mileage reports must be turned in. \n\nThe model answer covers the following key facts: \n- The vehicle is transported to the Swan Street location if it is not normally parked in Albany/Capital District. \n- All related items such as gas cards, Fleet Service cards/manuals, E-ZPass tags, and completed/signed mileage reports are turned in. \n\nThe model answer adds additional details not present in the reference answer, such as the removal of the vehicle from service, processing for auction, transfer, or disposal, and notifying concerned parties. None ITS employees can telecommute in several ways, including:\n\n1. Regularly Scheduled: Routine telecommuting arrangements with a set schedule.\n3. Exceptions: Telecommuting arrangements that exceed 50% of the telecommuter's regularly scheduled work hours in a pay period and requested on a temporary and ad hoc basis. These requests will be evaluated on a case-by-case basis.\n4. What is the purpose of the Use of Artificial Intelligence policy? The purpose of this policy is to establish guidelines for the acceptable use of Artificial Intelligence (AI) technologies, as defined here within, by State Entities (SE). None The Use of Artificial Intelligence policy is designed to establish guidelines for the responsible use of AI technologies by State Entities (SE). The policy aims to drive innovation, increase operational efficiencies, and better serve New Yorkers while protecting privacy, managing risk, and promoting accountability, safety, and equity. The policy applies to SEs, which include State Government as defined in Executive Order 117 or State Agencies as defined in Section 101 of the State Technology Law, and any third parties that use or access any IT Resource for which the SE or ITS has administrative responsibility. The policy applies to all technology systems that deploy AI technology, defined as a machine-based system that can make predictions, recommendations, or decisions influencing real or virtual environments. AI systems include but are not limited to systems that use machine learning, large language model, natural language processing, and computer vision technologies. The policy applies to all new and existing AI systems that are developed, used, or procured by SEs, that when used could directly impact the public. However, the policy does not govern SE's regulatory or other actions regarding non-agency uses of AI. SEs may adopt different policies, but they must include the requirements set forth in this one. Where a conflict exists between this policy/standard and a SE's policy, the more restrictive policy will take precedence. 4 The reference answer states that the purpose of the Use of Artificial Intelligence policy is to establish guidelines for the acceptable use of AI technologies by State Entities (SE). The model answer covers this key fact by stating that the policy is designed to establish guidelines for the responsible use of AI technologies by SEs. Overall, the model answer is mostly correct, accurate, and factual, as it aligns with the reference answer and provides additional relevant information.

What are the types of telecommuting for ITS employees? The types of telecommuting for ITS employees are event driven, regularly scheduled, and exception. ## 4.1 Types of Telecommuting\n\nEvent Driven - Occasional telecommuting arrangement that is infrequent and not regularly scheduled, which is approved or directed by the Division Executive, or their designee.\n\nRegularly Scheduled - Routine telecommuting arrangement with a set schedule.\n\nExceptions - A telecommuting arrangement that exceeds 50% of the telecommuter's regularly scheduled work hours in a pay period and requested on a temporary and adhoc basis. These requests will be evaluated on a case-by-case basis.\n\n## 4.2 Eligibility\n\nAll ITS employees may be eligible for the Telecommuting Program if the employee meets the following criteria:\n\nThe Telecommuting Program is completely voluntary. Every application will be considered on an individual basis. ITS reserves the right to unilaterally approve, disapprove, modify, revoke, or suspend any individual's participation in this program pursuant to procedures outlined in Section 4.3.5. Telecommuting is not operationally feasible for all job functions. The Bureau Director, or designee, determines which job functions are eligible to participate in this program. Determinations as to which job functions are eligible for telecommuting are final and cannot be appealed.\n\nThis program will sunset on June 30, 2025 but can be extended at the discretion of ITS. ITS will comply with any current or future obligations under collective bargaining agreements regarding telecommuting, including meeting with union representatives prior to the termination of the Telecommuting Program if required by the applicable collective bargaining agreement.\n\n## 4.1 Types of Telecommuting\n\nITS may provide telecommuters the necessary equipment and software, within reason, to telecommute. ITS will not provide desks, chairs, file cabinets, or other office-related furniture. The use of an employee's personal device (for example, desktop, laptop, tablet, etc.) requires the use of Virtual Desktop Infrastructure (VDI), Virtual Private Network (VPN), or access to email, OneDrive, and/or SharePoint via Outlook Web Access, all of which require multifactor authentication. The supervisor will determine which connection mechanism is appropriate based on operational need and the availability of resources. Telecommuters using personal devices must request, receive, and test any necessary software and authentication token prior to telecommuting. ITS will not be responsible for any hardware issues that may occur on personal devices because of the program. Telecommuters are responsible for keeping their personal devices functioning. The ITS Service Desk cannot answer calls and/or respond to tickets that are\n\nTelecommuters must be available via all required methods of communication throughout the workday. The telecommuter must comply with all applicable ITS and NYS policies and standards while telecommuting including, but not limited to NYS-P14-001 Acceptable Use of Information Technology Resources and ITSS23-002 Use of Personal Devices and Communication Channels.\n\nUnless otherwise directed by ITS, telecommuters will not be excused from work when a directed early departure or office closure is issued for the official work site.\n\nConversely, if an emergency occurs at the alternate work site and the telecommuter is unable to work at the telecommuting site that day or if the telecommuter is unable to, for any reason, continue working during the scheduled hours, the supervisor may direct the telecommuter to report to the officialwork site or grant appropriate charge to leave accruals.\n\n## 4.6.1.1 Exceptions The types of telecommuting for ITS employees are Event Driven, Regularly Scheduled, and Exceptions. Event Driven telecommuting is an occasional arrangement that is infrequent and not regularly scheduled. Regularly Scheduled telecommuting is a routine arrangement with a set schedule. Exceptions are a telecommuting arrangement that exceeds 50% of the telecommuter's regularly scheduled work hours in a pay period and requested on a temporary and adhoc basis. 5 The reference answer lists three types of telecommuting for ITS employees: event driven, regularly scheduled, and exception. The telecommuter may suspend or withdraw from telecommuting at any time with prior notice to the supervisor.\n\nEmployees who have been removed from the Telecommuting Program may reapply for participation no sooner than six months from the date of removal.\n\n## 4.4 Appeal Process\n\nIf an employee has their application denied, the employee may request a review by the Telecommuting Appeal Board within five (5) business days of receipt of the denial. The Telecommuting Appeal Board shall consist of a representative from ITS Division of Legal Affairs, ITS Office of Administration, and ITS Human Resources.\n\nThe employee will receive instructions through their ITS email on how to engage in the appeal process.\n\nITS may provide telecommuters the necessary equipment and software, within reason, to telecommute. ITS will not provide desks, chairs, file cabinets, or other office-related furniture. The use of an employee's personal device (for example, desktop, laptop, tablet, etc.) requires the use of Virtual Desktop Infrastructure (VDI), Virtual Private Network (VPN), or access to email, OneDrive, and/or SharePoint via Outlook Web Access, all of which require multifactor authentication. The supervisor will determine which connection mechanism is appropriate based on operational need and the availability of resources. Telecommuters using personal devices must request, receive, and test any necessary software and authentication token prior to telecommuting. ITS will not be responsible for any hardware issues that may occur on personal devices because of the program. Telecommuters are responsible for keeping their personal devices functioning. The ITS Service Desk cannot answer calls and/or respond to tickets that are No, ITS employees cannot telecommute if they have unsatisfactory performance. The supervisor should complete the HR-304 Unsatisfactory Telecommuting Report Form if there are issues with a telecommuter's productivity, responsiveness, workspace compliance, technology issues, or other reasons. The telecommuting agreement can be suspended or terminated for unsatisfactory performance. 5 The reference answer states that ITS employees cannot telecommute if they have unsatisfactory performance, which is determined by factors such as a satisfactory performance evaluation, work product, time and attendance record, and a lack of recent disciplinary history or counseling. The model answer correctly states that ITS employees cannot telecommute if they have unsatisfactory performance. The key fact from the reference answer, that satisfactory performance is required for telecommuting, is accurately covered in the model answer.
When does a new telecommuting period begin each year for ITS employees? July 1 marks the beginning of each new telecommuting period. ## 4.3.3 Renewal\n\nTelecommuters are required to retake the ITS Telecommuting Program training, How to Work Remotely training, and submit a new telecommuting application by July 1 annually, which marks the beginning of each new telecommuting period, to continue telecommuting.\n\n## 4.3.4 Work Plan\n\nThe supervisor will use the telecommuter's performance program, if applicable, in conjunction with current work assignments to define the performance and work productivity expectations for telecommuting days. The supervisor and telecommuter must discuss assignments and expectations (the "work plan") in advance of telecommuting and meet regularly to assess productivity and performance; adjustments to assignments and expectations should be made on an ongoing, as-needed basis. The supervisor shall ensure that the work plan is captured in writing in advance of, or no later than the start of, the telecommuting\n\nTelecommuters will treat telecommuting days like regular workdays and will be expected to maintain a regular work schedule and routine while telecommuting (including overtime when appropriate and authorized in advance). The same attendance rules and call-in procedures apply when telecommuting. Official work site coverage will be among the considerations made by the employee's supervisor when making telecommuting decisions. Seniority may be used as a factor in the approval of a telecommuting day.\n\nSupervisors shall require telecommuters to have a set telecommuting schedule. The approved set schedule is determined by the employee's supervisor based on operational needs. Any request for a change in an approved set schedule or telecommuting day must be submitted to the supervisor in advance.\n\nThe Telecommuting Program is completely voluntary. Every application will be considered on an individual basis. ITS reserves the right to unilaterally approve, disapprove, modify, revoke, or suspend any individual's participation in this program pursuant to procedures outlined in Section 4.3.5. Telecommuting is not operationally feasible for all job functions. The Bureau Director, or designee, determines which job functions are eligible to participate in this program. Determinations as to which job functions are eligible for telecommuting are final and cannot be appealed.\n\nThis program will sunset on June 30, 2025 but can be extended at the discretion of ITS. ITS will comply with any current or future obligations under collective bargaining agreements regarding telecommuting, including meeting with union representatives prior to the termination of the Telecommuting Program if required by the applicable collective bargaining agreement.\n\n## 4.1 Types of Telecommuting\n\n| 12/06/2023 | Revised to reflect changes in the telecommuting program. | Administration |\n| 07/05/2024 | Revised to reflect changes in the telecommuting program. | Administration | A new telecommuting period begins each year for ITS employees on July 1. Are the guidelines on the use of Open Source Software a policy or a standard? The Acceptable Use of Open Source Software, NYS-P19-005, is an NYS IT policy. <!-- image -->\n\nState Capitol P.O. Box 2062 Albany, NY 12220-0062 www.its.ny.gov\n\n## New York State Information Technology Policy\n\nIT Policy :\n\n## Acceptable Use of Open Source Software\n\nNo:\n\nITS-P19-005\n\nUpdated:\n\n03/25/2020\n\nIssued By:\n\nNYS Office of Information\n\nTechnology Services\n\nOwner:\n\nChief Technology Office\n\n## 1.0 Purpose and Benefits\n\nThis policy describes the acceptable use of Open-source software (OSS). The purpose is to maximize the impact and benefit of using OSS and to ensure that any technical, legal, or business risks resulting from that usage are properly mitigated. OSS provides an opportunity to reduce development and operational costs. Unlike other software, OSS makes its source code freely available to others who would like to view that code, copy it, learn from it, alter it, or share it.\n\n## 2.0 Authority\n\nAt minimum, OSS must meet these four (4) conditions to be reviewed:\n\n- 2. The source code of the software must be available on the Internet.\n- 1. The software must be free to use.\n- 3. The license to use the software must be approved by the ITS Division of Legal Affairs (DLA). A list of approved licenses is listed in Appendix A: Pre-Screened Open Source Licenses.\n- 4. The user is not required to agree to terms or conditions prior to the download; or, DLA has approved the terms and conditions associated with the OSS. 2\n\nOSS options should be considered first for all potential software solutions. A list of approved OSS can be accessed on the ITS Approved Software List.\n\n## 5.0 Compliance\n\nThis policy shall take effect upon publication. Compliance is required with all enterprise policies and standards. ITS may amend its policies and standards at any time; compliance with amended policies and standards is required.\n\n## 6.0 Definitions of Key Terms\n\n## 4.0 Information Statement\n\n## 4.1 Use of AI\n\nThe SE may use AI systems to further their mission and meet critical business needs. The use of AI, even if not subject to this policy, must be in compliance with applicable New York State and ITS policies and standards and New York and federal law. Particular attention should be made to the use of Open-Source AI to ensure compliance with ITS-P19-005: Acceptable Use of Open Source Software, where applicable. Additionally, SEs must maintain awareness of how the AI system uses personally identifiable, confidential, or sensitive information to ensure such use complies with applicable laws, rules, regulations, notices, and policies. SEs are required to have SE leadership approval prior to adopting new AI systems. Such approval should include SE executive legal and operational leadership, including the SE's ethics officer. 4\n\nStatewide technology policies, standards, and guidelines may be found at the following website: http://www.its.ny.gov/tables/technologypolicyindex\n\n## 8.0 Revision History\n\nThis standard shall be reviewed at least once every year to ensure relevancy. The guidelines on the use of Open Source Software are a policy. This is stated explicitly in the document's title, which is "New York State Information Technology Policy: Acceptable Use of Open Source Software" (ITS-P19-005). Additionally, the document outlines the authority, compliance requirements, and definitions of key terms, all of which are typical features of a policy. 5 The reference answer states that the 'Acceptable Use of Open Source Software, NYS-P19-005' is an NYS IT policy. What is a benefit ITS sees in Open-source software (OSS)? OSS provides an opportunity to reduce development and operational costs. <!-- image -->\n\nState Capitol P.O. OSS provides an opportunity to reduce development and operational costs. Section 102(2) of the State Technology Law gives the Director of ITS responsibility for the administration of ITS. Details regarding this authority can be found in New York State (NYS) ITS Policy, NYS-P08-002 Authority to Establish Enterprise Information Technology (IT) Policies, Standards and Guidelines .\n\n## 3.0 Scope\n\nThis policy document applies to ITS and its employees (including full-time, part-time, and temporary employees), contractors, consultants, volunteers, interns, and ITS supported agencies ("Client Agency").\n\n## 4.0 Information Statement\n\nOnly the ITS Chief Technology Officer (CTO) or an assigned designee may approve use of OSS. ITS shall keep an approved list of authorized designees.\n\nAt minimum, OSS must meet these four (4) conditions to be reviewed:\n\n- Provide work/life balance and leverage work capacity to enhance performance.\n- · Maintain an agency culture that supports employee flexibility and mobility.\n- · Promote resiliency during work site disruptions, including modified and suspended operations.\n- · Sustain the recruitment and retention of a high-quality workforce by providing a supportive and productive work environment.\n- · Contribute to a cleaner environment, reducing operational and transportation costs and travel time.\n\n## 2.0 Authority\n\nSection 1 of Executive Order No. 117 1 , established January 2002, charges the State Chief Information Officer with overseeing and supervising the management and operations of ITS . Section 102(2) of the State Technology Law gives the Director of ITS responsibility for the administration of ITS. Details regarding this authority can be found in NYS ITS Policy, NYS-P08-002 Authority to Establish Enterprise Information Technology (IT) Policies, Standards and Guidelines .\n\nITS-P10-003\n\nNo:\n\nUpdated:\n\n07/05/2024 ITS sees several benefits in Open-source software (OSS). First, OSS provides an opportunity to reduce development and operational costs. This is because the source code of OSS is freely available, which means that ITS does not have to pay for the software. Additionally, OSS allows ITS to leverage the work of a community of developers who are constantly improving and updating the software. This can lead to faster development times and more robust software.\n\nAnother benefit of OSS is that it can help ITS maintain an agency culture that supports employee flexibility and mobility. This is because OSS is often developed and maintained by a community of volunteers, which means that ITS can tap into a global pool of talent. This can help ITS attract and retain high-quality employees who are looking for a flexible and mobile work environment.\n\nFinally, OSS can help ITS promote resiliency during work site disruptions, including modified and suspended operations. This is because OSS is often available under an open license, which means that ITS can use the software even if the vendor goes out of business or stops supporting the software. This can help ITS ensure that its critical systems continue to operate even in the face of unexpected disruptions. 4 The reference answer highlights one key benefit of Open-source software (OSS) for ITS: the opportunity to reduce development and operational costs. The model answer covers this key point by stating that OSS provides an opportunity to reduce development and operational costs because the source code is freely available, which means ITS does not have to pay for the software. Additionally, the model answer expands on this by mentioning other benefits such as leveraging a community of developers for faster development times, maintaining a flexible and mobile work environment, and promoting resiliency during work site disruptions. While these additional points are not mentioned in the reference answer, they do not contradict it and provide further context and potential benefits of OSS. Therefore, the model answer is mostly correct, accurate, and factual in relation to the reference answer.

Will a user receive an alert when they leave a ny.gov website? Yes, when a link on a ny.gov Internet domain makes causes the user to leave a ny.gov Internet website, a notification or screen (i.e., a splash message) should alert users that they are leaving the official ny.gov Internet domain page. This requirement recognizes the proper performance of SE functions and includes an obligation for clear and unambiguous public notification of the SE's involvement in, or sponsorship of its information dissemination products including public websites. It also recognizes in certain limited circumstances other domains may be necessary for the proper performance of an SE function.\n\n## 4.6 Link Change Notification\n\nWhen a link on a ny.gov Internet domain makes causes the user to leave a ny.gov Internet website, a notification or screen (i.e., a splash message) should alert users that they are leaving the official ny.gov Internet domain page. When a link on a ny.gov domain makes the user go to another ny.gov domain, a notification or screen (i.e., a splash message) should not alert users that they are leaving the official ny.gov Internet domain page because the user is still within the ny.gov domain. (e.g., governor.ny.gov linking to its.ny.gov)\n\n## 4.7 New York State Government Entity Compliance\n\n## 4.7 New York State Government Entity Compliance\n\nEffective immediately, all new requests for state government entity Internet websites, and requests for domain names shall use domain names as described within this policy.\n\nThe following is required by all state government entities to be in compliance:\n\n- · Use of a ny.gov domain name for the state government entity's main public web site;\n- · State government entities must retire their legacy domain names immediately.\n- · Use of either ny.gov or the ITS approved ny.gov domain name for the primary website name must be provided on all documents, publications, correspondence, and public service information for the state government entity.\n\n## 4.8 Federal Government Compliance\n\nThe Federal Government can terminate or deny the use of an organization's dot-gov domain name where such websites are not operated in compliance with the conditions of use.\n\n## 5.0 Compliance\n\nOnce a domain has been determined and approved, the appropriate ITS Customer Relations Manager can submit a Service Request ticket to initiate the work required for set up in the ITSM service catalog: Network Services > DNS Entry.\n\n## 4.5 Use of Approved Domains.\n\nSEs should use only ny.gov domains. It is highly discouraged to use any other top-level domain unless the head of the SE explicitly determines another domain is necessary for the proper performance of an SE function. The use of any other domain runs the risk of the domain being lost or acquired by another entity. The ny.gov address ensures the public that it is an official state site and can be trusted.\n\nITS has secured the domain "ny.gov" for New York State government entity use.\n\n## 3.0 Scope\n\nThis policy applies to all "State Entities" (SE), defined as "State Government" in Executive Order 117 or "State Agencies" as defined in Section 101 of the State Technology Law. How long are dot-gov domains registered for? All dot-gov domains are registered for a 2-year period. ## 4.3.3 Two-Year Eligibility Period\n\nAll dot-gov domains are registered for a 2-year period. During this period, a review of eligibility and administrative information is required. If necessary, the dot-gov Registrar will contact the Administrative Point of Contact (APOC) for domains. APOC information MUST be kept current. The dot-gov Registrar may request an updated authorization letter, updated Domain Name Server (DNS) information, or other information. This information enables the federal government to ensure dot-gov domains provide secure, official websites and promote the best possible service to the general public.\n\n## 4.4 Procedure to Request a Domain Name\n\nSEs must obtain ITS approval before requesting any new third level domains (i.e., "agency\_name".ny.gov or "program\_name".ny.gov) using the form at https://on.ny.gov/domain-exception-request. ITS will review and respond to all requests within five (5) business days.\n\n## 4.3.2 No Political or Campaign Information\n\nThe dot-gov domain, and the ny.gov sub-domain, is for the sole operation of government, not for use in any political, political party, or campaign environment. No campaigning can be conducted with dot-gov domains. No dot-gov website may link, directly or indirectly, or refer to websites created or operated by a campaign or any campaign entity or political or campaign committee. Political sites, party names, or party acronyms cannot be used.\n\n## 4.3.3 Two-Year Eligibility Period\n\n## 4.7 New York State Government Entity Compliance\n\nEffective immediately, all new requests for state government entity Internet websites, and requests for domain names shall use domain names as described within this policy.\n\nThe following is required by all state government entities to be in compliance:\n\n- · Use of a ny.gov domain name for the state government entity's main public web site;\n- · State government entities must retire their legacy domain names immediately.\n- · Use of either ny.gov or the ITS approved ny.gov domain name for the primary website name must be provided on all documents, publications, correspondence, and public service information for the state government entity.\n\n## 4.8 Federal Government Compliance\n\nThe Federal Government can terminate or deny the use of an organization's dot-gov domain name where such websites are not operated in compliance with the conditions of use.\n\n## 5.0 Compliance\n\nOnce a domain has been determined and approved, the appropriate ITS Customer Relations Manager can submit a Service Request ticket to initiate the work required for set up in the ITSM service catalog: Network Services > DNS Entry.\n\n## 4.5 Use of Approved Domains.\n\nSEs should use only ny.gov domains. It is highly discouraged to use any other top-level domain unless the head of the SE explicitly determines another domain is necessary for the proper performance of an SE function. The use of any other domain runs the risk of the domain being lost or acquired by another entity. The ny.gov address ensures the public that it is an official state site and can be trusted. Dot-gov domains are registered for a 2-year period. This information is provided in the context under the section "4.3.3 Two-Year Eligibility Period." 5 The reference answer states that all dot-gov domains are registered for a 2-year period. The model answer correctly states that dot-gov domains are registered for a 2-year period, which matches the key fact in the reference answer. Additionally, the model answer provides extra context by mentioning the section '4.3.3 Two-Year Eligibility Period,' which does not contradict the reference answer. Therefore, the model answer is completely correct, accurate, and factual in relation to the reference answer.
What is the NYS ITS definition of Artificial Intelligence (AI)? AI is defined as a machine-based system that can, for a given set of human-defined objectives, make predictions, recommendations, or decisions influencing real or virtual environments. The definition includes but is not limited to systems that use machine learning, large language model, natural language processing, and computer vision technologies, including generative AI. ## 3.2 Definitions and Covered Use\n\nThis policy applies to all technology systems that deploy AI technology, hereafter referred to as "AI systems." For the purposes of this policy, AI is defined as a machinebased system that can, for a given set of human-defined objectives, make predictions, recommendations, or decisions influencing real or virtual environments. Artificial intelligence systems use machine- and human-based inputs to perceive real and virtual environments; abstract such perceptions into models through analysis in an automated manner; and use model inference to formulate options for information or action.\n\nThe definition includes but is not limited to systems that use machine learning, large language model, natural language processing, and computer vision technologies, including generative AI. 2 The definition does not include basic calculations, basic automation, or pre-recorded "if this then that (IFTT)" response systems.\n\n<!-- image -->\n\nState Capitol P.O. Are the guidelines on mobile device security for ITS employees a policy or a standard? The guidelines on mobile device sercurity, NYS-S14-009, is an NYS IT standard. - 1. As required by the NYS-S14-007 Encryption Standard, all mobile devices that access or contain any SE information must be encrypted.\n- 2. For State-issued mobile devices or personal mobile devices with direct access to SE private networks ( see NYS-S14-012 Bring Your Own Device Standard), only those applications which are approved by the SE may be installed and/or run on the mobile devices. Controls must be in place to both enforce SE application control requirements and prevent the installation of unauthorized or prohibited applications. Applications accessing SE data must be delivered either through the platform vendor's AppStore or State-authorized management systems.\n- 3. SE information must be removed or rendered inaccessible from mobile devices after no more than 10 incorrect authentication attempts.\n- 4. Mobile devices must automatically lock after being idle for a period not to exceed 10 minutes.\n\n- 7. Use of mobile device synchronization services, including backups (e.g., local device synchronization, remote synchronization services, and websites) must be controlled by the SE through an MDM or other centralized management solution.\n- 8. The mobile device's operating environment integrity must be verified (including whether the device has been rooted/jailbroken) prior to accessing SE private networks\n- 9. SEs must manage all mobile devices by:\n- a. Implementing mobile device policies and configurations as appropriate to the use of the mobile device.\n- b. Developing and implementing processes that check for upgrades and patches to the mobile device's software components, and for appropriately acquiring, testing, and deploying the updates to State-issued mobile devices, when technically possible.\n- c. Providing a mechanism to quarantine, or otherwise isolate, a mobile device from SE private networks or applications if it is below a minimum OS version or software patch level.\n\n## 9.0 Related Documents\n\nNIST Special Publication 800-124, Rev 1, Managing the Security of Mobile Devices in the Enterprise $\_{ }$\n\nDepartment of Homeland Security (DHS) Science & Technology (S&T) Directorate Mobile Device Security\n\n## 4.7 Security\n\nTelecommuters are responsible for adhering to all ITS policies and standards concerning the use of computer equipment and the security of data/information while telecommuting or while in transit between work sites, including but not limited to the ITS Acceptable Use of Information Technology Resources Policy (NYS-P14-001). These policies and standards can be found on Inside Edge. The guidelines on mobile device security for ITS employees are a standard. What is the Universal Navigation on NYS websites? The New York State Universal Navigation connects all NYS web sites to www.ny.gov both visually and interactively, enabling users to navigate government services from anywhere across the “NYS Web.” The Universal Navigation consists of header and footer navigation menus for use on SE public web sites. The Universal Navigation consists of header and footer navigation menus for use on SE public web sites. The Universal Navigation elements are to be placed on all SE public web sites and web applications as defined below.\n\n## 4.1 New York State Universal Navigation\n\nThe official embeddable code of the Universal Navigation and implementation instructions are found on the New York State GitHub account in the "Universal Navigation" repository.\n\nTo accommodate web sites with requirements that limit the standard functionality of the Universal Navigation, multiple versions may be included in the repository. Be sure to use the appropriate version for your site or application, following the instructions specific to that version. Guidelines or instructions included in the repository should be considered an extension of this standard.\n\nTo aid in implementation, the repository also contains guidance, frequently asked questions, demo versions, and other resources.\n\n## 4.2 Universal Navigation Size\n\n## 4.4 Placement of the Universal Navigation\n\nThe Universal Navigation must appear at the top of every page on the SE's public web sites and web applications. Nothing should appear above the Universal Navigation in the browser or application window except NYS translation functionality. No additional edits should be made to alter the appearance of the Universal Navigation, including additional links. No elements of the native web page or application should overlap the container element of the Universal Navigation.\n\n## 4.5 Intranet and Non-Public Facing Sites or Applications\n\nIf inclusion enhances the user experience, Intranet web sites, extranets, and other nonpublic facing sites or applications may include the Universal Navigation but are not required to do so.\n\n## 4.6 Functionality and Updates to the Universal Navigation\n\n## 4.2 Universal Navigation Size\n\nThe Universal Navigation is designed to extend the entire width of the webpage. Unless a specific exclusion is made based on a written request, the Universal Navigation should extend to the full width, with no space between the respective elements and the corresponding edges of the browser or application window. The elements use responsive design techniques to appropriately scale for different devices, including desktop computers, tablets, and mobile phones (provided the site or application was also designed in a responsive manner).\n\n## 4.3 Universal Navigation Color\n\nThe Universal Navigation is designed to blend with NYS sites and applications; hence colors of the Universal Navigation are not to be adjusted. Colors on existing web sites should continue to follow the established NYS Branding Guidelines.\n\n## 4.4 Placement of the Universal Navigation\n\n<!-- image -->\n\nState Capitol P.O. What does an employee need to provide in an appeal to the Telecommuting Appeal board? An employee needs to provide a request in writing to its.sm.Administration@its.ny.gov. This request must contain information regarding why the employee disagrees with the determination, along with any new information for the Appeal Board to consider. Individual telecommuting agreements may be suspended or terminated for any other reason at any time by the agency with thirty days' notice where feasible and consistent with agency operating needs. The telecommuter may suspend or withdraw from telecommuting at any time with prior notice to the supervisor.\n\nEmployees who have been removed from the Telecommuting Program may reapply for participation no sooner than six months from the date of removal.\n\n## 4.4 Appeal Process\n\nIf an employee has their application denied, the employee may request a review by the Telecommuting Appeal Board within five (5) business days of receipt of the denial. The Telecommuting Appeal Board shall consist of a representative from ITS Division of Legal Affairs, ITS Office of Administration, and ITS Human Resources.\n\nThe employee will receive instructions through their ITS email on how to engage in the appeal process.\n\n- · Requests must be made in writing to its.sm.Administration@its.ny.gov within five (5) business days of the denial.\n- · Requests must contain information regarding why the employee disagrees with the determination, along with any new information for the Appeal Board to consider.\n- · Appeals will generally be heard within ten (10) business days of receipt.\n- · Employees will be notified in writing of the Appeal Board's determination.\n\nDenials of applications for telecommuting under the Telecommuting Program are not grievable under any collective bargaining agreements. The employee may submit a new application six (6) months after the date of the appeal denial or earlier as determined by their supervisor.\n\n## 4.5 Reasonable Accommodations\n\n## 4.3.1 Training\n\nEmployees are required to take the ITS Telecommuting Program and How to Work Remotely trainings prior to applying for telecommuting. Supervisors/managers of employees applying for telecommuting must also take this training before reviewing or accepting applications. ITS reserves the right to periodically modify the training requirements.\n\n## 4.3.2 Application\n\nEmployees must submit a telecommuting application to be eligible for telecommuting.\n\nThe direct supervisor, with the approval of the second-level supervisor, has full discretion to either approve or deny an application for telecommuting. If denied, the employee may appeal the decision in writing as outlined in Section 4.4.\n\nThe supervisor may require an employee to submit a new telecommuting application if the employee leaves the current position or program area or if the employee's job duties or function significantly changes.\n\n## 4.3.3 Renewal\n\nWork Site;\n\n- 6. Will not violate any confidentiality agreement, policy or compliance obligation that may prohibit records or information from being removed from or accessed outside of their official work site.\n\nProbationary employees may be allowed to telecommute with supervisor approval.\n\n## 4.3 Request Process\n\nAn employee cannot begin telecommuting until the requirements set forth in this section are complete.\n\n## 4.3.1 Training In an appeal to the Telecommuting Appeal Board, an employee must provide information regarding why they disagree with the determination and any new information for the Appeal Board to consider. Who is on the Telecommuting Appeal Board? The telecommuting appeal board consists of a representative from ITS Division of Legal Affairs, ITS Office of Administration, and ITS Human Resources. Individual telecommuting agreements may be suspended or terminated for any other reason at any time by the agency with thirty days' notice where feasible and consistent with agency operating needs. The telecommuter may suspend or withdraw from telecommuting at any time with prior notice to the supervisor.\n\nEmployees who have been removed from the Telecommuting Program may reapply for participation no sooner than six months from the date of removal.\n\n## 4.4 Appeal Process\n\nIf an employee has their application denied, the employee may request a review by the Telecommuting Appeal Board within five (5) business days of receipt of the denial. The Telecommuting Appeal Board shall consist of a representative from ITS Division of Legal Affairs, ITS Office of Administration, and ITS Human Resources.\n\nThe employee will receive instructions through their ITS email on how to engage in the appeal process.\n\nThe Telecommuting Program is completely voluntary. Every application will be considered on an individual basis. ITS reserves the right to unilaterally approve, disapprove, modify, revoke, or suspend any individual's participation in this program pursuant to procedures outlined in Section 4.3.5. Telecommuting is not operationally feasible for all job functions. The Bureau Director, or designee, determines which job functions are eligible to participate in this program. Determinations as to which job functions are eligible for telecommuting are final and cannot be appealed.\n\nThis program will sunset on June 30, 2025 but can be extended at the discretion of ITS. ITS will comply with any current or future obligations under collective bargaining agreements regarding telecommuting, including meeting with union representatives prior to the termination of the Telecommuting Program if required by the applicable collective bargaining agreement.\n\n## 4.1 Types of Telecommuting\n\n## 4.3.1 Training\n\nEmployees are required to take the ITS Telecommuting Program and How to Work Remotely trainings prior to applying for telecommuting. ITS reserves the right to periodically modify the training requirements.\n\n## 4.3.2 Application\n\nEmployees must submit a telecommuting application to be eligible for telecommuting.\n\nThe direct supervisor, with the approval of the second-level supervisor, has full discretion to either approve or deny an application for telecommuting. If denied, the employee may appeal the decision in writing as outlined in Section 4.4.\n\nThe supervisor may require an employee to submit a new telecommuting application if the employee leaves the current position or program area or if the employee's job duties or function significantly changes.\n\n## 4.3.3 Renewal\n\n- · Requests must be made in writing to its.sm.Administration@its.ny.gov within five (5) business days of the denial.\n- · Requests must contain information regarding why the employee disagrees with the determination, along with any new information for the Appeal Board to consider.\n- · Appeals will generally be heard within ten (10) business days of receipt.\n- · Employees will be notified in writing of the Appeal Board's determination.\n\nDenials of applications for telecommuting under the Telecommuting Program are not grievable under any collective bargaining agreements. The employee may submit a new application six (6) months after the date of the appeal denial or earlier as determined by their supervisor.\n\n## 4.5 Reasonable Accommodations The Telecommuting Appeal Board consists of a representative from ITS Division of Legal Affairs, ITS Office of Administration, and ITS Human Resources. 5 The reference answer states that the Telecommuting Appeal Board consists of a representative from the ITS Division of Legal Affairs, ITS Office of Administration, and ITS Human Resources. Should SE websites have sub-domain addresses? SE websites should use short URLs over a separate or sub-domain address or areas on the same website. An example of this is health.ny.gov/flu instead of flu.health.ny.gov. Once a domain has been determined and approved, the appropriate ITS Customer Relations Manager can submit a Service Request ticket to initiate the work required for set up in the ITSM service catalog: Network Services > DNS Entry.\n\n## 4.5 Use of Approved Domains.\n\nSEs should use only ny.gov domains. It is highly discouraged to use any other top-level domain unless the head of the SE explicitly determines another domain is necessary for the proper performance of an SE function. The use of any other domain runs the risk of the domain being lost or acquired by another entity. The ny.gov address ensures the public that it is an official state site and can be trusted.\n\n- a) The SE is commonly known by the acronym, or\n- b) The acronym represents a commonly known major program. Major programs may be multiple or single agency programs but widely known to the general public. This program naming option is not intended for small, targeted audience programs. Web pages for such smaller programs must be part of the SE's main domain name pages (e.g., www.health.ny.gov/flu);\n- · Refrain from using general terms such as "licenses," "recreation," and "benefits" without an identifier because they do not represent a specific agency/program origin or service. For example, "DriversLicenses.ny.gov" may be allowed. Statewide services that would be best represented by a general term would be an infrequent exception to this rule (e.g., desktop.ny.gov, login.ny.gov).\n- · Use short URLs over a separate or sub-domain address, for areas on the same website (e.g., use health.ny.gov/flu instead of flu.health.ny.gov).\n\n- · Be easily understood and recognizable by the residents of New York State Clearly communicate the purpose of the site;\n- · Be easy to type and avoid using confusing characters such as zeroes (0) in place of the letter "O" or the number one (1) in place of the letter "L" (l).\n- · Contain no less than 10 but no more than 36 characters, including the ny.gov portion of the domain name (the "dots" are considered characters - hence subdomains of ny.gov are to have at least 3 characters)\n- · Contain letters, numbers and dashes (-), but no other special characters such as underscores (\_) and blank spaces;\n- · Avoid the use of acronyms whenever possible, unless the acronym meets one of the following conditions:\n- a) The SE is commonly known by the acronym, or\n\nITS has secured the domain "ny.gov" for New York State government entity use.\n\n## 3.0 Scope\n\nThis policy applies to all "State Entities" (SE), defined as "State Government" in Executive Order 117 or "State Agencies" as defined in Section 101 of the State Technology Law. This includes employees and all third parties (such as local governments, consultants, vendors, and contractors) that use or access any IT resource for which the SE or ITS has administrative responsibility, including systems managed or hosted by third parties on behalf of the SE or ITS. While an SE may adopt a different policy, it must include the requirements set forth in this one. Where a conflict exists between this policy/standard and a SE's policy, the more restrictive policy will take precedence.\n\n## 4.0 Information Statement\n\nAll SE websites will use a standard domain naming convention which is determined and enforced by ITS.\n\n## 4.1 Domain Naming Convention\n\nAll domain names must: No, SE websites should not have sub-domain addresses. The context emphasizes the use of short URLs over a separate or sub-domain address for areas on the same website. For example, it suggests using "health.ny.gov/flu" instead of "flu.health.ny.gov". This preference for short URLs is to ensure that the domain names are easily understood, recognizable, and easy to type for the residents of New York State. Additionally, the domain names should clearly communicate the purpose of the site and avoid confusing characters or special characters. 5 The reference answer states that SE websites should use short URLs over a separate or sub-domain address for areas on the same website, providing an example of 'health.ny.gov/flu' instead of 'flu.health.ny.gov'. The model answer covers these key facts by stating that SE websites should not have sub-domain addresses and emphasizes the preference for short URLs. It also provides the same example and explains the reasoning behind this preference, such as ensuring domain names are easily understood, recognizable, and easy to type. The model answer aligns well with the reference answer and adds additional context, which is acceptable.
When should SE domain names use acronyms? During this period, a review of eligibility and administrative information is required. If necessary, the dot-gov Registrar will contact the Administrative Point of Contact (APOC) for domains. APOC information MUST be kept current. The dot-gov Registrar may request an updated authorization letter, updated Domain Name Server (DNS) information, or other information. This information enables the federal government to ensure dot-gov domains provide secure, official websites and promote the best possible service to the general public.\n\n## 4.4 Procedure to Request a Domain Name\n\nSEs must obtain ITS approval before requesting any new third level domains (i.e., "agency\_name".ny.gov or "program\_name".ny.gov) using the form at https://on.ny.gov/domain-exception-request. ITS will review and respond to all requests within five (5) business days. SE domain names should use acronyms when the SE is commonly known by the acronym or when the acronym represents a commonly known major program. Major programs may be multiple or single agency programs but widely known to the general public. This program naming option is not intended for small, targeted audience programs. Web pages for such smaller programs must be part of the SE's main domain name pages (e.g., www.health.ny.gov/flu). 4 The reference answer provides two key facts: 1) SE domain names should avoid using acronyms unless the SE is commonly known by the acronym, and 2) acronyms can be used if they represent a commonly known major program. These additional details do not contradict the reference answer and provide further context. Therefore, the model answer is mostly correct, accurate, and factual.

The purpose is to maximize the impact and benefit of using OSS and to ensure that any technical, legal, or business risks resulting from that usage are properly mitigated. OSS provides an opportunity to reduce development and operational costs. Unlike other software, OSS makes its source code freely available to others who would like to view that code, copy it, learn from it, alter it, or share it.\n\n## 2.0 Authority\n\n## 4.6 Functionality and Updates to the Universal Navigation\n\nFunctionality of the Universal Navigation should be tested in a development environment before deploying. If problems exist when implementing the standard version, check in the repository for additional authorized versions that can be used until problems are resolved.\n\nUpdates to the Universal Navigation occur periodically. In general, a testing period will precede official deployment of updates. Test the updates in development environments and submit problems or concerns through the ITS Enterprise Information Technology Management System's ("ITSM") WebNY Enterprise Platform Services Bureau assignment group, L2 PLAT WEBNY SUPPORT.\n\n## 4.7 Including Accessibility Features Yes, OSS options should be considered first for all potential ITS software solutions. Unlike other software, OSS makes its source code freely available to others who would like to view that code, copy it, learn from it, alter it, or share it.\n\n## 2.0 Authority\n\n## 5.0 Compliance\n\nThis policy shall take effect upon publication. What is the purpose of the Use of Artificial Intelligence policy? The purpose of this policy is to establish guidelines for the acceptable use of Artificial Intelligence (AI) technologies, as defined here within, by State Entities (SE). This policy applies to all new and existing AI systems that are developed, used or procured by SEs, that when used could directly impact the public. 3\n\nThe policy does not govern SE's regulatory or other actions regarding non-agency uses of AI.\n\n## 4.0 Information Statement\n\n## 4.1 Use of AI\n\n## 3.2 Definitions and Covered Use\n\nThis policy applies to all technology systems that deploy AI technology, hereafter referred to as "AI systems." For the purposes of this policy, AI is defined as a machinebased system that can, for a given set of human-defined objectives, make predictions, recommendations, or decisions influencing real or virtual environments. Artificial intelligence systems use machine- and human-based inputs to perceive real and virtual environments; abstract such perceptions into models through analysis in an automated manner; and use model inference to formulate options for information or action.\n\nThe definition includes but is not limited to systems that use machine learning, large language model, natural language processing, and computer vision technologies, including generative AI. 2 The definition does not include basic calculations, basic automation, or pre-recorded "if this then that (IFTT)" response systems.\n\n<!-- image -->\n\nState Capitol P.O. Through the responsible use of AI, SEs can drive innovation, increase operational efficiencies, and better serve New Yorkers while protecting privacy, managing risk, and promoting accountability, safety, and equity. Agencies are encouraged to responsibly adopt AI technologies and should consider this policy a tool to aid in that adoption.\n\n## 2.0 Authority\n\n| Machine Learning | Using AI systems to provide insights in support of human decision making. Are the guidelines on the use of Artificial Intelligence a policy or a standard? The Acceptable Use of Articial Intelligence Technologies, NYS-P24-001, is an NYS IT policy. ## 3.2 Definitions and Covered Use\n\nThis policy applies to all technology systems that deploy AI technology, hereafter referred to as "AI systems." For the purposes of this policy, AI is defined as a machinebased system that can, for a given set of human-defined objectives, make predictions, recommendations, or decisions influencing real or virtual environments. Artificial intelligence systems use machine- and human-based inputs to perceive real and virtual environments; abstract such perceptions into models through analysis in an automated manner; and use model inference to formulate options for information or action.\n\nThe definition includes but is not limited to systems that use machine learning, large language model, natural language processing, and computer vision technologies, including generative AI. 2 The definition does not include basic calculations, basic automation, or pre-recorded "if this then that (IFTT)" response systems.\n\nThis policy applies to all new and existing AI systems that are developed, used or procured by SEs, that when used could directly impact the public. 3\n\nThe policy does not govern SE's regulatory or other actions regarding non-agency uses of AI.\n\n## 4.0 Information Statement\n\n## 4.1 Use of AI\n\nThe SE must identify an Information Owner for each AI system that meets the criteria set forth in Section 3.2. For examples of acceptable and unacceptable uses of AI systems, please see Appendix A to this policy.\n\n## 4.2 Human Oversight\n\nAI systems aid and enhance human decision making that may impact the public. SEs must ensure that decisions that impact the public are not made without oversight by appropriate staff, who make the final decisions. Automated final decision systems are not permitted.\n\nSEs shall take steps to ensure that where AI systems are used to aid in decision making that impacts the public, the outcomes, decisions, and supporting methodologies of such AI systems are documented appropriately. 5 The Information Owner is responsible for periodically assessing the outputs of their in-production AI systems to validate continuing reliability, safety, and fairness.\n\n## 4.3 Fairness and Equity, and Explain Ability\n\n## 4.3 Fairness and Equity, and Explain Ability\n\nUse of AI systems should be fair and equitable in accordance with applicable State and Federal laws, rules, and regulations. Systemic, computational, and human biases should be identified and remediated.\n\nAll AI systems should be explainable to the maximum extent practicable.\n\n## 4.4 Transparency\n\nTransparency is an important principle of AI governance. Where members of the public interact directly with SE systems that use AI technology, the use of such AI technology should be disclosed by the SE. 6\n\n## 4.5 AI Risk Assessment and Management The guidelines on the use of Artificial Intelligence are a policy. This is stated in the context when it mentions "This policy applies to all technology systems that deploy AI technology, hereafter referred to as 'AI systems.'" The policy outlines the definitions, covered use, and requirements for the use of AI systems in SEs. 5 The reference answer states that the guidelines on the use of Artificial Intelligence are an NYS IT policy, specifically named 'The Acceptable Use of Artificial Intelligence Technologies, NYS-P24-001.' The model answer correctly identifies the guidelines as a policy and provides additional context by mentioning that it applies to all technology systems deploying AI technology and outlines definitions, covered use, and requirements. Therefore, the model answer is completely correct, accurate, and factual.

Is there a centralized ITS warehouse to store equipments? No there is not a centralized ITS warehouse to store eqipment. Business units are responsible for storing items. ## 4.1 E-Equipment\n\nE-equipment is hardware used to input, store, process, transmit, and output information, including, but not limited to, desktops, laptops, mobile devices, servers, mobile devices, video conferencing equipment, copiers, printers, and data center equipment. The business unit must follow the Chief Technology Office's (CTO) guidelines for disposition of end of life E-equipment and NYS-S13-003 Sanitization/Secure Disposal Standard. Once properly prepared for surplus or disposal, the business unit must submit a ITSM ServiceNow Surplus/LDA Service Request.\n\nAs established in, ITS-P21-001 Workplace Computing Device and ITS-P18-007 Mobile Provisioning and Deprovision policies, it is the responsibility of the Client Agency to properly return devices, including E-equipment, no longer needed, and to coordinate with agency legal counsel regarding preservation obligations before turning over equipment to ITS.\n\nITS Facilities Services will work with the business unit to review the form. If the form is complete, ITS Facilities Services will approve and authorize the disposal of furniture or miscellaneous equipment. If the form is incomplete, it will be returned to the requestor for revision. Furniture and miscellaneous equipment cannot be removed without the proper approval and authorization as indicated above.\n\nIn all cases, until a final determination is made by ITS Facilities Services, the business unit is responsible for storing items. There is no ITS centralized warehouse area to hold furniture or miscellaneous equipment.\n\n## 4.3 Vehicles\n\nWhen a business unit determines a State Vehicle should be removed from service, the business unit must notify ITS Facilities Services. If the vehicle is determined to be reusable, ITS Facilities Services will deploy it to a new location. If ITS Facilities Services determines the vehicle will be surplused, the following actions are to be taken:\n\nIf the furniture or miscellaneous equipment is determined to have value but is no longer needed for ITS use (i.e., items that are still in reasonably good shape and/or still function properly but are no longer needed by the business unit), a CS-201 Form must be completed and, if applicable, the Information Security Certification must be signed. The completed form, along with digital pictures, must be sent to ITS Facilities Services at its.sm.surplus@its.ny.gov, for authorization and processing. Once all approvals are in place, ITS Facilities Services will coordinate the furniture or miscellaneous equipment drop-off with OGS.\n\nIn order to effectively surplus and dispose of items no longer of use, and which have no value, the ITS surplus and disposal process has been established based on guidelines provided by the Office of General Services (OGS) and NYS-S13-003 Sanitization/Secure Disposal Standard.\n\n## 2.0 Authority\n\nSection 103(10) of the State Technology Law provides ITS with the authority to establish statewide technology policies, including technology and security standards. What are the types of telecommuting for ITS employees? The types of telecommuting for ITS employees are event driven, regularly scheduled, and exception. ## 4.1 Types of Telecommuting\n\nEvent Driven - Occasional telecommuting arrangement that is infrequent and not regularly scheduled, which is approved or directed by the Division Executive, or their designee.\n\nRegularly Scheduled - Routine telecommuting arrangement with a set schedule.\n\nExceptions - A telecommuting arrangement that exceeds 50% of the telecommuter's regularly scheduled work hours in a pay period and requested on a temporary and adhoc basis. These requests will be evaluated on a case-by-case basis.\n\n## 4.2 Eligibility\n\nAll ITS employees may be eligible for the Telecommuting Program if the employee meets the following criteria:\n\nThe Telecommuting Program is completely voluntary. Every application will be considered on an individual basis. ITS reserves the right to unilaterally approve, disapprove, modify, revoke, or suspend any individual's participation in this program pursuant to procedures outlined in Section 4.3.5. Telecommuting is not operationally feasible for all job functions. The Bureau Director, or designee, determines which job functions are eligible to participate in this program. Determinations as to which job functions are eligible for telecommuting are final and cannot be appealed.\n\nThis program will sunset on June 30, 2025 but can be extended at the discretion of ITS. ITS will comply with any current or future obligations under collective bargaining agreements regarding telecommuting, including meeting with union representatives prior to the termination of the Telecommuting Program if required by the applicable collective bargaining agreement.\n\n## 4.1 Types of Telecommuting\n\nITS may provide telecommuters the necessary equipment and software, within reason, to telecommute. ITS will not provide desks, chairs, file cabinets, or other office-related furniture. The use of an employee's personal device (for example, desktop, laptop, tablet, etc.) requires the use of Virtual Desktop Infrastructure (VDI), Virtual Private Network (VPN), or access to email, OneDrive, and/or SharePoint via Outlook Web Access, all of which require multifactor authentication. The supervisor will determine which connection mechanism is appropriate based on operational need and the availability of resources. Telecommuters using personal devices must request, receive, and test any necessary software and authentication token prior to telecommuting. ITS will not be responsible for any hardware issues that may occur on personal devices because of the program. Telecommuters are responsible for keeping their personal devices functioning. The ITS Service Desk cannot answer calls and/or respond to tickets that are\n\nTelecommuters must be available via all required methods of communication throughout the workday. The telecommuter must comply with all applicable ITS and NYS policies and standards while telecommuting including, but not limited to NYS-P14-001 Acceptable Use of Information Technology Resources and ITSS23-002 Use of Personal Devices and Communication Channels.\n\nUnless otherwise directed by ITS, telecommuters will not be excused from work when a directed early departure or office closure is issued for the official work site.\n\nConversely, if an emergency occurs at the alternate work site and the telecommuter is unable to work at the telecommuting site that day or if the telecommuter is unable to, for any reason, continue working during the scheduled hours, the supervisor may direct the telecommuter to report to the officialwork site or grant appropriate charge to leave accruals.\n\n## 4.6.1.1 Exceptions The types of telecommuting for ITS employees are:\n\n1. Event Driven: This is an occasional telecommuting arrangement that is infrequent and not regularly scheduled. It is approved or directed by the Division Executive or their designee.\n\n2. Regularly Scheduled: This is a routine telecommuting arrangement with a set schedule.\n\n3. Exceptions: This is a telecommuting arrangement that exceeds 50% of the telecommuter's regularly scheduled work hours in a pay period and is requested on a temporary and adhoc basis. These requests are evaluated on a case-by-case basis.\n\nITS may provide necessary equipment and software for telecommuting, but not office-related furniture. Telecommuters using personal devices must use Virtual Desktop Infrastructure (VDI), Virtual Private Network (VPN), or access to email, OneDrive, and/or SharePoint via Outlook Web Access, all of which require multifactor authentication. Telecommuters are responsible for keeping their personal devices functioning and must be available via all required methods of communication throughout the workday. They must also comply with all applicable ITS and NYS policies and standards while telecommuting. 5 The reference answer lists three types of telecommuting for ITS employees: event driven, regularly scheduled, and exception. The model answer covers all three types: 'Event Driven', 'Regularly Scheduled', and 'Exceptions'. When does a new telecommuting period begin each year for ITS employees? July 1 marks the beginning of each new telecommuting period. ## 4.3.3 Renewal\n\nTelecommuters are required to retake the ITS Telecommuting Program training, How to Work Remotely training, and submit a new telecommuting application by July 1 annually, which marks the beginning of each new telecommuting period, to continue telecommuting.\n\n## 4.3.4 Work Plan\n\nThe supervisor will use the telecommuter's performance program, if applicable, in conjunction with current work assignments to define the performance and work productivity expectations for telecommuting days. The supervisor and telecommuter must discuss assignments and expectations (the "work plan") in advance of telecommuting and meet regularly to assess productivity and performance; adjustments to assignments and expectations should be made on an ongoing, as-needed basis. The supervisor shall ensure that the work plan is captured in writing in advance of, or no later than the start of, the telecommuting\n\nTelecommuters will treat telecommuting days like regular workdays and will be expected to maintain a regular work schedule and routine while telecommuting (including overtime when appropriate and authorized in advance). The same attendance rules and call-in procedures apply when telecommuting. Official work site coverage will be among the considerations made by the employee's supervisor when making telecommuting decisions. Seniority may be used as a factor in the approval of a telecommuting day.\n\nSupervisors shall require telecommuters to have a set telecommuting schedule. The approved set schedule is determined by the employee's supervisor based on operational needs. Any request for a change in an approved set schedule or telecommuting day must be submitted to the supervisor in advance.\n\nThe Telecommuting Program is completely voluntary. Every application will be considered on an individual basis. ITS reserves the right to unilaterally approve, disapprove, modify, revoke, or suspend any individual's participation in this program pursuant to procedures outlined in Section 4.3.5. Telecommuting is not operationally feasible for all job functions. The Bureau Director, or designee, determines which job functions are eligible to participate in this program. Determinations as to which job functions are eligible for telecommuting are final and cannot be appealed.\n\nThis program will sunset on June 30, 2025 but can be extended at the discretion of ITS. Are the guidelines on the use of Open Source Software a policy or a standard? The Acceptable Use of Open Source Software, NYS-P19-005, is an NYS IT policy. <!-- image -->\n\nState Capitol P.O. Box 2062 Albany, NY 12220-0062 www.its.ny.gov\n\n## New York State Information Technology Policy\n\nIT Policy :\n\n## Acceptable Use of Open Source Software\n\nNo:\n\nITS-P19-005\n\nUpdated:\n\n03/25/2020\n\nIssued By:\n\nNYS Office of Information\n\nTechnology Services\n\nOwner:\n\nChief Technology Office\n\n## 1.0 Purpose and Benefits\n\nThis policy describes the acceptable use of Open-source software (OSS). The purpose is to maximize the impact and benefit of using OSS and to ensure that any technical, legal, or business risks resulting from that usage are properly mitigated. OSS provides an opportunity to reduce development and operational costs. Unlike other software, OSS makes its source code freely available to others who would like to view that code, copy it, learn from it, alter it, or share it.\n\n## 2.0 Authority\n\nAt minimum, OSS must meet these four (4) conditions to be reviewed:\n\n- 2. The source code of the software must be available on the Internet.\n- 1. The software must be free to use.\n- 3. The license to use the software must be approved by the ITS Division of Legal Affairs (DLA). A list of approved licenses is listed in Appendix A: Pre-Screened Open Source Licenses.\n- 4. The user is not required to agree to terms or conditions prior to the download; or, DLA has approved the terms and conditions associated with the OSS. 2\n\nOSS options should be considered first for all potential software solutions. A list of approved OSS can be accessed on the ITS Approved Software List.\n\n## 5.0 Compliance\n\nThis policy shall take effect upon publication. Compliance is required with all enterprise policies and standards. ITS may amend its policies and standards at any time; compliance with amended policies and standards is required.\n\n## 6.0 Definitions of Key Terms\n\n## 4.0 Information Statement\n\n## 4.1 Use of AI\n\nThe SE may use AI systems to further their mission and meet critical business needs. The use of AI, even if not subject to this policy, must be in compliance with applicable New York State and ITS policies and standards and New York and federal law. Particular attention should be made to the use of Open-Source AI to ensure compliance with ITS-P19-005: Acceptable Use of Open Source Software, where applicable. Additionally, SEs must maintain awareness of how the AI system uses personally identifiable, confidential, or sensitive information to ensure such use complies with applicable laws, rules, regulations, notices, and policies. SEs are required to have SE leadership approval prior to adopting new AI systems. Such approval should include SE executive legal and operational leadership, including the SE's ethics officer. 4\n\nStatewide technology policies, standards, and guidelines may be found at the following website: http://www.its.ny.gov/tables/technologypolicyindex\n\n## 8.0 Revision History\n\nThis standard shall be reviewed at least once every year to ensure relevancy. The guidelines on the use of Open Source Software are a policy, specifically ITS-P19-005: Acceptable Use of Open Source Software. This is indicated by the "Policy" label in the document title and the section numbering starting from 1.0 (which typically denotes the start of a policy document). 5 The reference answer states that the 'Acceptable Use of Open Source Software, NYS-P19-005' is an NYS IT policy. The model answer correctly identifies the guidelines as a policy, specifically naming it as 'ITS-P19-005: Acceptable Use of Open Source Software.' The model answer provides additional details, such as the document title and section numbering, to support its claim that it is a policy. These details do not contradict the reference answer and are consistent with it. Therefore, the model answer is completely correct, accurate, and factual in relation to the reference answer.

Section 102(2) of the State Technology Law gives the Director of ITS responsibility for the administration of ITS. Details regarding this authority can be found in New York State (NYS) ITS Policy, NYS-P08-002 Authority to Establish Enterprise Information Technology (IT) Policies, Standards and Guidelines .\n\n## 3.0 Scope\n\nThis policy document applies to ITS and its employees (including full-time, part-time, and temporary employees), contractors, consultants, volunteers, interns, and ITS supported agencies ("Client Agency").\n\n## 4.0 Information Statement\n\nOnly the ITS Chief Technology Officer (CTO) or an assigned designee may approve use of OSS. ITS shall keep an approved list of authorized designees.\n\nAt minimum, OSS must meet these four (4) conditions to be reviewed:\n\n- Provide work/life balance and leverage work capacity to enhance performance.\n- · Maintain an agency culture that supports employee flexibility and mobility.\n- · Promote resiliency during work site disruptions, including modified and suspended operations.\n- · Sustain the recruitment and retention of a high-quality workforce by providing a supportive and productive work environment.\n- · Contribute to a cleaner environment, reducing operational and transportation costs and travel time.\n\n## 2.0 Authority\n\nSection 1 of Executive Order No. 117 1 , established January 2002, charges the State Chief Information Officer with overseeing and supervising the management and operations of ITS . Section 102(2) of the State Technology Law gives the Director of ITS responsibility for the administration of ITS. Unlike proprietary software, OSS makes its source code freely available, allowing users to view, copy, learn from, alter, or share it. The license to use the software must be approved by the ITS Division of Legal Affairs (DLA). A list of approved licenses is listed in Appendix A: Pre-Screened Open Source Licenses.\n- 4. The user is not required to agree to terms or conditions prior to the download; or, DLA has approved the terms and conditions associated with the OSS. 2\n\nOSS options should be considered first for all potential software solutions. Will a user receive an alert when they leave a ny.gov website? Yes, when a link on a ny.gov Internet domain makes causes the user to leave a ny.gov Internet website, a notification or screen (i.e., a splash message) should alert users that they are leaving the official ny.gov Internet domain page. This requirement recognizes the proper performance of SE functions and includes an obligation for clear and unambiguous public notification of the SE's involvement in, or sponsorship of its information dissemination products including public websites. It also recognizes in certain limited circumstances other domains may be necessary for the proper performance of an SE function.\n\n## 4.6 Link Change Notification\n\nWhen a link on a ny.gov Internet domain makes causes the user to leave a ny.gov Internet website, a notification or screen (i.e., a splash message) should alert users that they are leaving the official ny.gov Internet domain page. When a link on a ny.gov domain makes the user go to another ny.gov domain, a notification or screen (i.e., a splash message) should not alert users that they are leaving the official ny.gov Internet domain page because the user is still within the ny.gov domain. (e.g., governor.ny.gov linking to its.ny.gov)\n\n## 4.7 New York State Government Entity Compliance\n\n## 4.7 New York State Government Entity Compliance\n\nEffective immediately, all new requests for state government entity Internet websites, and requests for domain names shall use domain names as described within this policy.\n\nThe following is required by all state government entities to be in compliance:\n\n- · Use of a ny.gov domain name for the state government entity's main public web site;\n- · State government entities must retire their legacy domain names immediately.\n- · Use of either ny.gov or the ITS approved ny.gov domain name for the primary website name must be provided on all documents, publications, correspondence, and public service information for the state government entity.\n\n## 4.8 Federal Government Compliance\n\nThe Federal Government can terminate or deny the use of an organization's dot-gov domain name where such websites are not operated in compliance with the conditions of use.\n\n## 5.0 Compliance\n\nOnce a domain has been determined and approved, the appropriate ITS Customer Relations Manager can submit a Service Request ticket to initiate the work required for set up in the ITSM service catalog: Network Services > DNS Entry.\n\n## 4.5 Use of Approved Domains.\n\nSEs should use only ny.gov domains. It is highly discouraged to use any other top-level domain unless the head of the SE explicitly determines another domain is necessary for the proper performance of an SE function. The use of any other domain runs the risk of the domain being lost or acquired by another entity. The ny.gov address ensures the public that it is an official state site and can be trusted.\n\nITS has secured the domain "ny.gov" for New York State government entity use.\n\n## 3.0 Scope\n\nThis policy applies to all "State Entities" (SE), defined as "State Government" in Executive Order 117 or "State Agencies" as defined in Section 101 of the State Technology Law. This includes employees and all third parties (such as local governments, consultants, vendors, and contractors) that use or access any IT resource for which the SE or ITS has administrative responsibility, including systems managed or hosted by third parties on behalf of the SE or ITS. While an SE may adopt a different policy, it must include the requirements set forth in this one. Where a conflict exists between this policy/standard and a SE's policy, the more restrictive policy will take precedence.\n\n## 4.0 Information Statement\n\nAll SE websites will use a standard domain naming convention which is determined and enforced by ITS.\n\n## 4.1 Domain Naming Convention\n\nAll domain names must: Yes, a user will receive an alert or a splash message when they leave a ny.gov website.
